{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01U3dNMn3QXa9KKMNWuK8LgA","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"1: /*\\n2:  * Licensed to the Apache Software Foundation (ASF) under one or more\\n3:  * contributor license agreements. See the NOTICE file distributed with\\n4:  * this work for additional information regarding copyright ownership.\\n5:  * The ASF licenses this file to You under the Apache License, Version 2.0\\n6:  * (the \\\"License\\\"); you may not use this file except in compliance with\\n7:  * the License. You may obtain a copy of the License at\\n8:  *\\n9:  *    http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\\n10:  *\\n11:  * Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\\n12:  * distributed under the License is distributed on an \\\"AS IS\\\" BASIS,\\n13:  * WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\\n14:  * See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\\n15:  * limitations under the License.\\n16:  */\\n17: package org.apache.kafka.clients.consumer;\\n18: \\n19: import org.apache.kafka.common.TopicPartition;\\n20: \\n21: import java.util.Collection;\\n22: \\n23: /**\\n24:  * A callback interface that the user can implement to trigger custom actions when the set of partitions assigned to the\\n25:  * consumer changes.\\n26:  * <p>\\n27:  * This is applicable when the consumer is having Kafka auto-manage group membership. If the consumer directly assigns partitions,\\n28:  * those partitions will never be reassigned and this callback is not applicable.\\n29:  * <p>\\n30:  * When Kafka is managing the group membership, a partition re-assignment will be triggered any time the members of the group change or the subscription\\n31:  * of the members changes. This can occur when processes die, new process instances are added or old instances come back to life after failure.\\n32:  * Partition re-assignments can also be triggered by changes affecting the subscribed topics (e.g. when the number of partitions is\\n33:  * administratively adjusted).\\n34:  * <p>\\n35:  * There are many uses for this functionality. One common use is saving offsets in a custom store. By saving offsets in\\n36:  * the {@link #onPartitionsRevoked(Collection)} call we can ensure that any time partition assignment changes\\n37:  * the offset gets saved.\\n38:  * <p>\\n39:  * Another use is flushing out any kind of cache of intermediate results the consumer may be keeping. For example,\\n40:  * consider a case where the consumer is subscribed to a topic containing user page views, and the goal is to count the\\n41:  * number of page views per user for each five minute window. Let's say the topic is partitioned by the user id so that\\n42:  * all events for a particular user go to a single consumer instance. The consumer can keep in memory a running\\n43:  * tally of actions per user and only flush these out to a remote data store when its cache gets too big. However if a\\n44:  * partition is reassigned it may want to automatically trigger a flush of this cache, before the new owner takes over\\n45:  * consumption.\\n46:  * <p>\\n47:  * This callback will only execute in the user thread as part of the {@link Consumer#poll(java.time.Duration) poll(long)} call\\n48:  * whenever partition assignment changes.\\n49:  * <p>\\n50:  * Under normal conditions, if a partition is reassigned from one consumer to another, then the old consumer will\\n51:  * always invoke {@link #onPartitionsRevoked(Collection) onPartitionsRevoked} for that partition prior to the new consumer\\n52:  * invoking {@link #onPartitionsAssigned(Collection) onPartitionsAssigned} for the same partition. So if offsets or other state is saved in the\\n53:  * {@link #onPartitionsRevoked(Collection) onPartitionsRevoked} call by one consumer member, it will always be accessible by the time the\\n54:  * other consumer member taking over that partition and triggering its {@link #onPartitionsAssigned(Collection) onPartitionsAssigned} callback to load the state.\\n55:  * <p>\\n56:  * You can think of revocation as a graceful way to give up ownership of a partition. In some cases, the consumer may not have an opportunity to do so.\\n57:  * For example, if the session times out, then the partitions may be reassigned before we have a chance to revoke them gracefully.\\n58:  * For this case, we have a third callback {@link #onPartitionsLost(Collection)}. The difference between this function and\\n59:  * {@link #onPartitionsRevoked(Collection)} is that upon invocation of {@link #onPartitionsLost(Collection)}, the partitions\\n60:  * may already be owned by some other members in the group and therefore users would not be able to commit its consumed offsets for example.\\n61:  * Users could implement these two functions differently (by default,\\n62:  * {@link #onPartitionsLost(Collection)} will be calling {@link #onPartitionsRevoked(Collection)} directly); for example, in the\\n63:  * {@link #onPartitionsLost(Collection)} we should not need to store the offsets since we know these partitions are no longer owned by the consumer\\n64:  * at that time.\\n65:  * <p>\\n66:  * During a rebalance event, the {@link #onPartitionsAssigned(Collection) onPartitionsAssigned} function will always be triggered exactly once when\\n67:  * the rebalance completes. That is, even if there is no newly assigned partitions for a consumer member, its {@link #onPartitionsAssigned(Collection) onPartitionsAssigned}\\n68:  * will still be triggered with an empty collection of partitions. As a result this function can be used also to notify when a rebalance event has happened.\\n69:  * With eager rebalancing, {@link #onPartitionsRevoked(Collection)} will always be called at the start of a rebalance. On the other hand, {@link #onPartitionsLost(Collection)}\\n70:  * will only be called when there were non-empty partitions that were lost.\\n71:  * With cooperative rebalancing, {@link #onPartitionsRevoked(Collection)} and {@link #onPartitionsLost(Collection)}\\n72:  * will only be triggered when there are non-empty partitions revoked or lost from this consumer member during a rebalance event.\\n73:  * <p>\\n74:  * It is possible\\n75:  * for a {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.WakeupException} or {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.InterruptException}\\n76:  * to be raised from one of these nested invocations. In this case, the exception will be propagated to the current\\n77:  * invocation of {@link KafkaConsumer#poll(java.time.Duration)} in which this callback is being executed. This means it is not\\n78:  * necessary to catch these exceptions and re-attempt to wakeup or interrupt the consumer thread.\\n79:  * Also if the callback function implementation itself throws an exception, this exception will be propagated to the current\\n80:  * invocation of {@link KafkaConsumer#poll(java.time.Duration)} as well.\\n81:  * <p>\\n82:  * Note that callbacks only serve as notification of an assignment change.\\n83:  * They cannot be used to express acceptance of the change.\\n84:  * Hence throwing an exception from a callback does not affect the assignment in any way,\\n85:  * as it will be propagated all the way up to the {@link KafkaConsumer#poll(java.time.Duration)} call.\\n86:  * If user captures the exception in the caller, the callback is still assumed successful and no further retries will be attempted.\\n87:  * <p>\\n88:  *\\n89:  * Here is pseudo-code for a callback implementation for saving offsets:\\n90:  * <pre>\\n91:  * {@code\\n92:  *   public class SaveOffsetsOnRebalance implements ConsumerRebalanceListener {\\n93:  *       private Consumer<?,?> consumer;\\n94:  *\\n95:  *       public SaveOffsetsOnRebalance(Consumer<?,?> consumer) {\\n96:  *           this.consumer = consumer;\\n97:  *       }\\n98:  *\\n99:  *       public void onPartitionsRevoked(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions) {\\n100:  *           // save the offsets in an external store using some custom code not described here\\n101:  *           for(TopicPartition partition: partitions)\\n102:  *              saveOffsetInExternalStore(consumer.position(partition));\\n103:  *       }\\n104:  *\\n105:  *       public void onPartitionsLost(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions) {\\n106:  *           // do not need to save the offsets since these partitions are probably owned by other consumers already\\n107:  *       }\\n108:  *\\n109:  *       public void onPartitionsAssigned(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions) {\\n110:  *           // read the offsets from an external store using some custom code not described here\\n111:  *           for(TopicPartition partition: partitions)\\n112:  *              consumer.seek(partition, readOffsetFromExternalStore(partition));\\n113:  *       }\\n114:  *   }\\n115:  * }\\n116:  * </pre>\\n117:  */\\n118: public interface ConsumerRebalanceListener {\\n119: \\n120:     /**\\n121:      * A callback method the user can implement to provide handling of offset commits to a customized store.\\n122:      * This method will be called during a rebalance operation when the consumer has to give up some partitions.\\n123:      * The consumer may need to give up some partitions (thus this callback executed) under the following scenarios:\\n124:      * <ul>\\n125:      *     <li>If the consumer assignment changes</li>\\n126:      *     <li>If the consumer is being closed ({@link KafkaConsumer#close(CloseOptions option)})</li>\\n127:      *     <li>If the consumer is unsubscribing ({@link KafkaConsumer#unsubscribe()})</li>\\n128:      * </ul>\\n129:      * It is recommended that offsets should be committed in this callback to either Kafka or a\\n130:      * custom offset store to prevent duplicate data.\\n131:      * <p>\\n132:      * This callback is always called before re-assigning the partitions.\\n133:      * If the consumer is using the {@link GroupProtocol#CLASSIC} rebalance protocol:\\n134:      * <ul>\\n135:      *     <li>\\n136:      *         In eager rebalancing, onPartitionsRevoked will be called with the full set of assigned partitions as a parameter (all partitions are revoked).\\n137:      *         It will be called even if there are no partitions to revoke.\\n138:      *     </li>\\n139:      *     <li>\\n140:      *         In cooperative rebalancing, onPartitionsRevoked will be called with the set of partitions to revoke,\\n141:      *         iff the set is non-empty.\\n142:      *     </li>\\n143:      * </ul>\\n144:      * If the consumer is using the {@link GroupProtocol#CONSUMER} rebalance protocol, this callback will be called\\n145:      * with the set of partitions to revoke iff the set is non-empty\\n146:      * (same behavior as the {@link GroupProtocol#CLASSIC} rebalance protocol with Cooperative mode).\\n147:      * <p>\\n148:      * For examples on usage of this API, see Usage Examples section of {@link KafkaConsumer KafkaConsumer}.\\n149:      * <p>\\n150:      * It is common for the revocation callback to use the consumer instance in order to commit offsets. It is possible\\n151:      * for a {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.WakeupException} or {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.InterruptException}\\n152:      * to be raised from one of these nested invocations. In this case, the exception will be propagated to the current\\n153:      * invocation of {@link KafkaConsumer#poll(java.time.Duration)} in which this callback is being executed. This means it is not\\n154:      * necessary to catch these exceptions and re-attempt to wakeup or interrupt the consumer thread.\\n155:      *\\n156:      * @param partitions The list of partitions that were assigned to the consumer and now need to be revoked. This will\\n157:      *                  include the full assignment under the Classic/Eager protocol, given that it revokes all partitions.\\n158:      *                   It will only include the subset to revoke under the Classic/Cooperative and Consumer protocols.\\n159:      * @throws org.apache.kafka.common.errors.WakeupException If raised from a nested call to {@link KafkaConsumer}\\n160:      * @throws org.apache.kafka.common.errors.InterruptException If raised from a nested call to {@link KafkaConsumer}\\n161:      */\\n162:     void onPartitionsRevoked(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions);\\n163: \\n164:     /**\\n165:      * A callback method the user can implement to provide handling of customized offsets on completion of a successful\\n166:      * partition re-assignment. This method will be called after the partition re-assignment completes (even if no new\\n167:      * partitions were assigned to the consumer), and before the consumer starts fetching data,\\n168:      * and only as the result of a {@link Consumer#poll(java.time.Duration) poll(long)} call.\\n169:      * <p>\\n170:      * It is guaranteed that under normal conditions all the processes in a consumer group will execute their\\n171:      * {@link #onPartitionsRevoked(Collection)} callback before any instance executes this onPartitionsAssigned callback.\\n172:      * During exceptional scenarios, partitions may be migrated\\n173:      * without the old owner being notified (i.e. their {@link #onPartitionsRevoked(Collection)} callback not triggered),\\n174:      * and later when the old owner consumer realized this event, the {@link #onPartitionsLost(Collection)} callback\\n175:      * will be triggered by the consumer then.\\n176:      * <p>\\n177:      * It is common for the assignment callback to use the consumer instance in order to query offsets. It is possible\\n178:      * for a {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.WakeupException} or {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.InterruptException}\\n179:      * to be raised from one of these nested invocations. In this case, the exception will be propagated to the current\\n180:      * invocation of {@link KafkaConsumer#poll(java.time.Duration)} in which this callback is being executed. This means it is not\\n181:      * necessary to catch these exceptions and re-attempt to wakeup or interrupt the consumer thread.\\n182:      *\\n183:      * @param partitions Partitions that have been added to the assignment as a result of the rebalance.\\n184:      *                   Note that partitions that were already owned by this consumer and remain assigned are not\\n185:      *                   included in this list under the Classic/Cooperative or Consumer protocols. THe full assignment\\n186:      *                   will be received under the Classic/Eager protocol.\\n187:      * @throws org.apache.kafka.common.errors.WakeupException    If raised from a nested call to {@link KafkaConsumer}\\n188:      * @throws org.apache.kafka.common.errors.InterruptException If raised from a nested call to {@link KafkaConsumer}\\n189:      */\\n190:     void onPartitionsAssigned(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions);\\n191: \\n192:     /**\\n193:      * A callback method you can implement to provide handling of cleaning up resources for partitions that have already\\n194:      * been reassigned to other consumers. This method will not be called during normal execution as the owned partitions would\\n195:      * first be revoked by calling the {@link ConsumerRebalanceListener#onPartitionsRevoked}, before being reassigned\\n196:      * to other consumers during a rebalance event. However, during exceptional scenarios when the consumer realized that it\\n197:      * does not own this partition any longer, i.e. not revoked via a normal rebalance event, then this method would be invoked.\\n198:      * <p>\\n199:      * For example, this function is called if a consumer's session timeout has expired, or if a fatal error has been\\n200:      * received indicating the consumer is no longer part of the group.\\n201:      * <p>\\n202:      * By default it will just trigger {@link ConsumerRebalanceListener#onPartitionsRevoked}; for users who want to distinguish\\n203:      * the handling logic of revoked partitions v.s. lost partitions, they can override the default implementation.\\n204:      * <p>\\n205:      * It is possible\\n206:      * for a {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.WakeupException} or {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.InterruptException}\\n207:      * to be raised from one of these nested invocations. In this case, the exception will be propagated to the current\\n208:      * invocation of {@link KafkaConsumer#poll(java.time.Duration)} in which this callback is being executed. This means it is not\\n209:      * necessary to catch these exceptions and re-attempt to wakeup or interrupt the consumer thread.\\n210:      *\\n211:      * @param partitions The list of partitions that were assigned to the consumer and now have been reassigned\\n212:      *                   to other consumers. With both, the Classic and Consumer protocols, this will always include\\n213:      *                   all partitions that were previously assigned to the consumer.\\n214:      * @throws org.apache.kafka.common.errors.WakeupException    If raised from a nested call to {@link KafkaConsumer}\\n215:      * @throws org.apache.kafka.common.errors.InterruptException If raised from a nested call to {@link KafkaConsumer}\\n216:      */\\n217:     default void onPartitionsLost(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions) {\\n218:         onPartitionsRevoked(partitions);\\n219:     }\\n220: }\\n221: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kafka--e678b4b@47ac12bd6042edf23f1dbca3d789db945d62802d/-/blob/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/ConsumerRebalanceListener.java\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"e1e96863-4dd1-457a-9aaf-69ff79f5231b","uuid":"87ada158-56c2-4194-83e8-a75a3d3541bd","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: /*\\n2:  * Licensed to the Apache Software Foundation (ASF) under one or more\\n3:  * contributor license agreements. See the NOTICE file distributed with\\n4:  * this work for additional information regarding copyright ownership.\\n5:  * The ASF licenses this file to You under the Apache License, Version 2.0\\n6:  * (the \\\"License\\\"); you may not use this file except in compliance with\\n7:  * the License. You may obtain a copy of the License at\\n8:  *\\n9:  *    http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\\n10:  *\\n11:  * Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\\n12:  * distributed under the License is distributed on an \\\"AS IS\\\" BASIS,\\n13:  * WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\\n14:  * See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\\n15:  * limitations under the License.\\n16:  */\\n17: package org.apache.kafka.clients.consumer;\\n18: \\n19: import org.apache.kafka.common.TopicPartition;\\n20: \\n21: import java.util.Collection;\\n22: \\n23: /**\\n24:  * A callback interface that the user can implement to trigger custom actions when the set of partitions assigned to the\\n25:  * consumer changes.\\n26:  * <p>\\n27:  * This is applicable when the consumer is having Kafka auto-manage group membership. If the consumer directly assigns partitions,\\n28:  * those partitions will never be reassigned and this callback is not applicable.\\n29:  * <p>\\n30:  * When Kafka is managing the group membership, a partition re-assignment will be triggered any time the members of the group change or the subscription\\n31:  * of the members changes. This can occur when processes die, new process instances are added or old instances come back to life after failure.\\n32:  * Partition re-assignments can also be triggered by changes affecting the subscribed topics (e.g. when the number of partitions is\\n33:  * administratively adjusted).\\n34:  * <p>\\n35:  * There are many uses for this functionality. One common use is saving offsets in a custom store. By saving offsets in\\n36:  * the {@link #onPartitionsRevoked(Collection)} call we can ensure that any time partition assignment changes\\n37:  * the offset gets saved.\\n38:  * <p>\\n39:  * Another use is flushing out any kind of cache of intermediate results the consumer may be keeping. For example,\\n40:  * consider a case where the consumer is subscribed to a topic containing user page views, and the goal is to count the\\n41:  * number of page views per user for each five minute window. Let's say the topic is partitioned by the user id so that\\n42:  * all events for a particular user go to a single consumer instance. The consumer can keep in memory a running\\n43:  * tally of actions per user and only flush these out to a remote data store when its cache gets too big. However if a\\n44:  * partition is reassigned it may want to automatically trigger a flush of this cache, before the new owner takes over\\n45:  * consumption.\\n46:  * <p>\\n47:  * This callback will only execute in the user thread as part of the {@link Consumer#poll(java.time.Duration) poll(long)} call\\n48:  * whenever partition assignment changes.\\n49:  * <p>\\n50:  * Under normal conditions, if a partition is reassigned from one consumer to another, then the old consumer will\\n51:  * always invoke {@link #onPartitionsRevoked(Collection) onPartitionsRevoked} for that partition prior to the new consumer\\n52:  * invoking {@link #onPartitionsAssigned(Collection) onPartitionsAssigned} for the same partition. So if offsets or other state is saved in the\\n53:  * {@link #onPartitionsRevoked(Collection) onPartitionsRevoked} call by one consumer member, it will always be accessible by the time the\\n54:  * other consumer member taking over that partition and triggering its {@link #onPartitionsAssigned(Collection) onPartitionsAssigned} callback to load the state.\\n55:  * <p>\\n56:  * You can think of revocation as a graceful way to give up ownership of a partition. In some cases, the consumer may not have an opportunity to do so.\\n57:  * For example, if the session times out, then the partitions may be reassigned before we have a chance to revoke them gracefully.\\n58:  * For this case, we have a third callback {@link #onPartitionsLost(Collection)}. The difference between this function and\\n59:  * {@link #onPartitionsRevoked(Collection)} is that upon invocation of {@link #onPartitionsLost(Collection)}, the partitions\\n60:  * may already be owned by some other members in the group and therefore users would not be able to commit its consumed offsets for example.\\n61:  * Users could implement these two functions differently (by default,\\n62:  * {@link #onPartitionsLost(Collection)} will be calling {@link #onPartitionsRevoked(Collection)} directly); for example, in the\\n63:  * {@link #onPartitionsLost(Collection)} we should not need to store the offsets since we know these partitions are no longer owned by the consumer\\n64:  * at that time.\\n65:  * <p>\\n66:  * During a rebalance event, the {@link #onPartitionsAssigned(Collection) onPartitionsAssigned} function will always be triggered exactly once when\\n67:  * the rebalance completes. That is, even if there is no newly assigned partitions for a consumer member, its {@link #onPartitionsAssigned(Collection) onPartitionsAssigned}\\n68:  * will still be triggered with an empty collection of partitions. As a result this function can be used also to notify when a rebalance event has happened.\\n69:  * With eager rebalancing, {@link #onPartitionsRevoked(Collection)} will always be called at the start of a rebalance. On the other hand, {@link #onPartitionsLost(Collection)}\\n70:  * will only be called when there were non-empty partitions that were lost.\\n71:  * With cooperative rebalancing, {@link #onPartitionsRevoked(Collection)} and {@link #onPartitionsLost(Collection)}\\n72:  * will only be triggered when there are non-empty partitions revoked or lost from this consumer member during a rebalance event.\\n73:  * <p>\\n74:  * It is possible\\n75:  * for a {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.WakeupException} or {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.InterruptException}\\n76:  * to be raised from one of these nested invocations. In this case, the exception will be propagated to the current\\n77:  * invocation of {@link KafkaConsumer#poll(java.time.Duration)} in which this callback is being executed. This means it is not\\n78:  * necessary to catch these exceptions and re-attempt to wakeup or interrupt the consumer thread.\\n79:  * Also if the callback function implementation itself throws an exception, this exception will be propagated to the current\\n80:  * invocation of {@link KafkaConsumer#poll(java.time.Duration)} as well.\\n81:  * <p>\\n82:  * Note that callbacks only serve as notification of an assignment change.\\n83:  * They cannot be used to express acceptance of the change.\\n84:  * Hence throwing an exception from a callback does not affect the assignment in any way,\\n85:  * as it will be propagated all the way up to the {@link KafkaConsumer#poll(java.time.Duration)} call.\\n86:  * If user captures the exception in the caller, the callback is still assumed successful and no further retries will be attempted.\\n87:  * <p>\\n88:  *\\n89:  * Here is pseudo-code for a callback implementation for saving offsets:\\n90:  * <pre>\\n91:  * {@code\\n92:  * {\\n96:  *           this.consumer = consumer;\\n97:  *       }\\n98:  *\\n99:  *       public void onPartitionsRevoked(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions) {\\n100:  *           // save the offsets in an external store using some custom code not described here\\n101:  *           for(TopicPartition partition: partitions)\\n102:  *              saveOffsetInExternalStore(consumer.position(partition));\\n103:  *       }\\n104:  *\\n105:  *       public void onPartitionsLost(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions) {\\n106:  *           // do not need to save the offsets since these partitions are probably owned by other consumers already\\n107:  *       }\\n108:  *\\n109:  *       public void onPartitionsAssigned(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions) {\\n110:  *           // read the offsets from an external store using some custom code not described here\\n111:  *           for(TopicPartition partition: partitions)\\n112:  *              consumer.seek(partition, readOffsetFromExternalStore(partition));\\n113:  *       }\\n114:  *   }\\n115:  * }\\n116:  * </pre>\\n117:  */\\n118: public interface ConsumerRebalanceListener {\\n119: \\n120:     /**\\n121:      * A callback method the user can implement to provide handling of offset commits to a customized store.\\n122:      * This method will be called during a rebalance operation when the consumer has to give up some partitions.\\n123:      * The consumer may need to give up some partitions (thus this callback executed) under the following scenarios:\\n124:      * <ul>\\n125:      *     <li>If the consumer assignment changes</li>\\n126:      *     <li>If the consumer is being closed ({@link KafkaConsumer#close(CloseOptions option)})</li>\\n127:      *     <li>If the consumer is unsubscribing ({@link KafkaConsumer#unsubscribe()})</li>\\n128:      * </ul>\\n129:      * It is recommended that offsets should be committed in this callback to either Kafka or a\\n130:      * custom offset store to prevent duplicate data.\\n131:      * <p>\\n132:      * This callback is always called before re-assigning the partitions.\\n133:      * If the consumer is using the {@link GroupProtocol#CLASSIC} rebalance protocol:\\n134:      * <ul>\\n135:      *     <li>\\n136:      *         In eager rebalancing, onPartitionsRevoked will be called with the full set of assigned partitions as a parameter (all partitions are revoked).\\n137:      *         It will be called even if there are no partitions to revoke.\\n138:      *     </li>\\n139:      *     <li>\\n140:      *         In cooperative rebalancing, onPartitionsRevoked will be called with the set of partitions to revoke,\\n141:      *         iff the set is non-empty.\\n142:      *     </li>\\n143:      * </ul>\\n144:      * If the consumer is using the {@link GroupProtocol#CONSUMER} rebalance protocol, this callback will be called\\n145:      * with the set of partitions to revoke iff the set is non-empty\\n146:      * (same behavior as the {@link GroupProtocol#CLASSIC} rebalance protocol with Cooperative mode).\\n147:      * <p>\\n148:      * For examples on usage of this API, see Usage Examples section of {@link KafkaConsumer KafkaConsumer}.\\n149:      * <p>\\n150:      * It is common for the revocation callback to use the consumer instance in order to commit offsets. It is possible\\n151:      * for a {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.WakeupException} or {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.InterruptException}\\n152:      * to be raised from one of these nested invocations. In this case, the exception will be propagated to the current\\n153:      * invocation of {@link KafkaConsumer#poll(java.time.Duration)} in which this callback is being executed. This means it is not\\n154:      * necessary to catch these exceptions and re-attempt to wakeup or interrupt the consumer thread.\\n155:      *\\n156:      * @param partitions The list of partitions that were assigned to the consumer and now need to be revoked. This will\\n157:      *                  include the full assignment under the Classic/Eager protocol, given that it revokes all partitions.\\n158:      *                   It will only include the subset to revoke under the Classic/Cooperative and Consumer protocols.\\n159:      * @throws org.apache.kafka.common.errors.WakeupException If raised from a nested call to {@link KafkaConsumer}\\n160:      * @throws org.apache.kafka.common.errors.InterruptException If raised from a nested call to {@link KafkaConsumer}\\n161:      */\\n162:     void onPartitionsRevoked(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions);\\n163: \\n164:     /**\\n165:      * A callback method the user can implement to provide handling of customized offsets on completion of a successful\\n166:      * partition re-assignment. This method will be called after the partition re-assignment completes (even if no new\\n167:      * partitions were assigned to the consumer), and before the consumer starts fetching data,\\n168:      * and only as the result of a {@link Consumer#poll(java.time.Duration) poll(long)} call.\\n169:      * <p>\\n170:      * It is guaranteed that under normal conditions all the processes in a consumer group will execute their\\n171:      * {@link #onPartitionsRevoked(Collection)} callback before any instance executes this onPartitionsAssigned callback.\\n172:      * During exceptional scenarios, partitions may be migrated\\n173:      * without the old owner being notified (i.e. their {@link #onPartitionsRevoked(Collection)} callback not triggered),\\n174:      * and later when the old owner consumer realized this event, the {@link #onPartitionsLost(Collection)} callback\\n175:      * will be triggered by the consumer then.\\n176:      * <p>\\n177:      * It is common for the assignment callback to use the consumer instance in order to query offsets. It is possible\\n178:      * for a {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.WakeupException} or {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.InterruptException}\\n179:      * to be raised from one of these nested invocations. In this case, the exception will be propagated to the current\\n180:      * invocation of {@link KafkaConsumer#poll(java.time.Duration)} in which this callback is being executed. This means it is not\\n181:      * necessary to catch these exceptions and re-attempt to wakeup or interrupt the consumer thread.\\n182:      *\\n183:      * @param partitions Partitions that have been added to the assignment as a result of the rebalance.\\n184:      *                   Note that partitions that were already owned by this consumer and remain assigned are not\\n185:      *                   included in this list under the Classic/Cooperative or Consumer protocols. THe full assignment\\n186:      *                   will be received under the Classic/Eager protocol.\\n187:      * @throws org.apache.kafka.common.errors.WakeupException    If raised from a nested call to {@link KafkaConsumer}\\n188:      * @throws org.apache.kafka.common.errors.InterruptException If raised from a nested call to {@link KafkaConsumer}\\n189:      */\\n190:     void onPartitionsAssigned(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions);\\n191: \\n192:     /**\\n193:      * A callback method you can implement to provide handling of cleaning up resources for partitions that have already\\n194:      * been reassigned to other consumers. This method will not be called during normal execution as the owned partitions would\\n195:      * first be revoked by calling the {@link ConsumerRebalanceListener#onPartitionsRevoked}, before being reassigned\\n196:      * to other consumers during a rebalance event. handling of offset commits to a customized store.\n122:      * This method will be called during a rebalance operation when the consumer has to give up some partitions.\n123:      * The consumer may need to give up some partitions (thus this callback executed) under the following scenarios:\n124:      * <ul>\n125:      *     <li>If the consumer assignment changes</li>\n126:      *     <li>If the consumer is being closed ({@link KafkaConsumer#close(CloseOptions option)})</li>\n127:      *     <li>If the consumer is unsubscribing ({@link KafkaConsumer#unsubscribe()})</li>\n128:      * </ul>\n129:      * It is recommended that offsets should be committed in this callback to either Kafka or a\n130:      * custom offset store to prevent duplicate data.\n131:      * <p>\n132:      * This callback is always called before re-assigning the partitions.\n133:      * If the consumer is using the {@link GroupProtocol#CLASSIC} rebalance protocol:\n134:      * <ul>\n135:      *     <li>\n136:      *         In eager rebalancing, onPartitionsRevoked will be called with the full set of assigned partitions as a parameter (all partitions are revoked).\n137:      *         It will be called even if there are no partitions to revoke.\n138:      *     </li>\n139:      *     <li>\n140:      *         In cooperative rebalancing, onPartitionsRevoked will be called with the set of partitions to revoke,\n141:      *         iff the set is non-empty.\n142:      *     </li>\n143:      * </ul>\n144:      * If the consumer is using the {@link GroupProtocol#CONSUMER} rebalance protocol, this callback will be called\n145:      * with the set of partitions to revoke iff the set is non-empty\n146:      * (same behavior as the {@link GroupProtocol#CLASSIC} rebalance protocol with Cooperative mode).\n147:      * <p>\n148:      * For examples on usage of this API, see Usage Examples section of {@link KafkaConsumer KafkaConsumer}.\n149:      * <p>\n150:      * It is common for the revocation callback to use the consumer instance in order to commit offsets. It is possible\n151:      * for a {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.WakeupException} or {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.InterruptException}\n152:      * to be raised from one of these nested invocations. In this case, the exception will be propagated to the current\n153:      * invocation of {@link KafkaConsumer#poll(java.time.Duration)} in which this callback is being executed. This means it is not\n154:      * necessary to catch these exceptions and re-attempt to wakeup or interrupt the consumer thread.\n155:      *\n156:      * @param partitions The list of partitions that were assigned to the consumer and now need to be revoked. This will\n157:      *                  include the full assignment under the Classic/Eager protocol, given that it revokes all partitions.\n158:      *                   It will only include the subset to revoke under the Classic/Cooperative and Consumer protocols.\n159:      * @throws org.apache.kafka.common.errors.WakeupException If raised from a nested call to {@link KafkaConsumer}\n160:      * @throws org.apache.kafka.common.errors.InterruptException If raised from a nested call to {@link KafkaConsumer}\n161:      */\n162:     void onPartitionsRevoked(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions);\n163: \n164:     /**\n165:      * A callback method the user can implement to provide handling of customized offsets on completion of a successful\n166:      * partition re-assignment. This method will be called after the partition re-assignment completes (even if no new\n167:      * partitions were assigned to the consumer), and before the consumer starts fetching data,\n168:      * and only as the result of a {@link Consumer#poll(java.time.Duration) poll(long)} call.\n169:      * <p>\n170:      * It is guaranteed that under normal conditions all the processes in a consumer group will execute their\n171:      * {@link #onPartitionsRevoked(Collection)} callback before any instance executes this onPartitionsAssigned callback.\n172:      * During exceptional scenarios, partitions may be migrated\n173:      * without the old owner being notified (i.e. their {@link #onPartitionsRevoked(Collection)} callback not triggered),\n174:      * and later when the old owner consumer realized this event, the {@link #onPartitionsLost(Collection)} callback\n175:      * will be triggered by the consumer then.\n176:      * <p>\n177:      * It is common for the assignment callback to use the consumer instance in order to query offsets. It is possible\n178:      * for a {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.WakeupException} or {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.InterruptException}\n179:      * to be raised from one of these nested invocations. In this case, the exception will be propagated to the current\n180:      * invocation of {@link KafkaConsumer#poll(java.time.Duration)} in which this callback is being executed. This means it is not\n181:      * necessary to catch these exceptions and re-attempt to wakeup or interrupt the consumer thread.\n182:      *\n183:      * @param partitions Partitions that have been added to the assignment as a result of the rebalance.\n184:      *                   Note that partitions that were already owned by this consumer and remain assigned are not\n185:      *                   included in this list under the Classic/Cooperative or Consumer protocols. THe full assignment\n186:      *                   will be received under the Classic/Eager protocol.\n187:      * @throws org.apache.kafka.common.errors.WakeupException    If raised from a nested call to {@link KafkaConsumer}\n188:      * @throws org.apache.kafka.common.errors.InterruptException If raised from a nested call to {@link KafkaConsumer}\n189:      */\n190:     void onPartitionsAssigned(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions);\n191: \n192:     /**\n193:      * A callback method you can implement to provide handling of cleaning up resources for partitions that have already\n194:      * been reassigned to other consumers. This method will not be called during normal execution as the owned partitions would\n195:      * first be revoked by calling the {@link ConsumerRebalanceListener#onPartitionsRevoked}, before being reassigned\n196:      * to other consumers during a rebalance event. However, during exceptional scenarios when the consumer realized that it\n197:      * does not own this partition any longer, i.e. not revoked via a normal rebalance event, then this method would be invoked.\n198:      * <p>\n199:      * For example, this function is called if a consumer's session timeout has expired, or if a fatal error has been\n200:      * received indicating the consumer is no longer part of the group.\n201:      * <p>\n202:      * By default it will just trigger {@link ConsumerRebalanceListener#onPartitionsRevoked}; for users who want to distinguish\n203:      * the handling logic of revoked partitions v.s. lost partitions, they can override the default implementation.\n204:      * <p>\n205:      * It is possible\n206:      * for a {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.WakeupException} or {@link org.apache.kafka.common.errors.InterruptException}\n207:      * to be raised from one of these nested invocations. In this case, the exception will be propagated to the current\n208:      * invocation of {@link KafkaConsumer#poll(java.time.Duration)} in which this callback is being executed. This means it is not\n209:      * necessary to catch these exceptions and re-attempt to wakeup or interrupt the consumer thread.\n210:      *\n211:      * @param partitions The list of partitions that were assigned to the consumer and now have been reassigned\n212:      *                   to other consumers. With both, the Classic and Consumer protocols, this will always include\n213:      *                   all partitions that were previously assigned to the consumer.\n214:      * @throws org.apache.kafka.common.errors.WakeupException    If raised from a nested call to {@link KafkaConsumer}\n215:      * @throws org.apache.kafka.common.errors.InterruptException If raised from a nested call to {@link KafkaConsumer}\n216:      */\n217:     default void onPartitionsLost(Collection<TopicPartition> partitions) {\n218:         onPartitionsRevoked(partitions);\n219:     }\n220: }\n221: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/kafka--e678b4b@47ac12bd6042edf23f1dbca3d789db945d62802d/-/blob/clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/clients/consumer/ConsumerRebalanceListener.java"}}}
